    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8622661303376139290"><b>Business in North Korea: a paradoxical and fascinating situation is interpreted by a true insider.</b><br/><br/>In 2002, the Swiss-Swedish power company ABB appointed Felix Abt its country director for North Korea. The Swiss Entrepreneur lived and worked in North Korea for seven years, one of the few foreign businessmen there. After the experience, Abt felt compelled to write <i>A Capitali</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8622661303376139290" style="display:none"><b>Business in North Korea: a paradoxical and fascinating situation is interpreted by a true insider.</b><br /><br />In 2002, the Swiss-Swedish power company ABB appointed Felix Abt its country director for North Korea. The Swiss Entrepreneur lived and worked in North Korea for seven years, one of the few foreign businessmen there. After the experience, Abt felt compelled to write <i>A Capitalist in North Korea</i> to describe the multifaceted society he encountered.<br /><br /> North Korea, at the time, was heavily sanctioned by the UN, which made it extremely difficult to do business. Yet, he discovered that it was a place where plastic surgery and South Korean TV dramas were wildly popular and where he rarely needed to walk more than a block to grab a quick hamburger. He was closely monitored, and once faced accusations of spying, yet he learned that young North Koreans are hopeful - signing up for business courses in anticipation of a brighter, more open, future. In <i>A Capitalist in North Korea</i>, Abt shares these and many other unusual facts and insights about one of the world's most secretive nations.<br /><br />Author Felix Abt is a politically neutral businessman and, therefore, does not share partisan views about North Korea. He is, however, critical of unfair North Korea reporting and does what he can to contribute to a more objective view of a country he knows much better than the journalists and bloggers writing about it. <br /><br />Abt is a former investor at several legitimate Joint Venture companies in North Korea which are now being driven into bankruptcy by U.N. "sanctions."</span>
  <a data-text-id="8622661303376139290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_809872323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/809872323" />
    <a title="Pesach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27279039-pesach"><img alt="Pesach" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/809872323?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pesach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pesach" href="/user/show/27279039-pesach">Pesach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/17255166-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people interested in North Korea, business people, people loving adventure</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Pesach by: </span>
      friends who loved the book
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer809872323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17152015466367801293">THIS BOOK is truly different from all other North Korea books I have read so far and offers a completely new perspective from a human (and humanistic) point of view, trying to show life in the country without political or ideological coloring.<br/><br/>Indeed, unlike other authors Felix Abt prefers to stay apolitical and impartial when sharing his thoughts and memories of his extraordinary seven-year sojourn. His unbiased approach to North Korea is a provocation to all those who read and believe the wacky</span>
  <span id="freeText17152015466367801293" style="display:none">THIS BOOK is truly different from all other North Korea books I have read so far and offers a completely new perspective from a human (and humanistic) point of view, trying to show life in the country without political or ideological coloring.<br /><br />Indeed, unlike other authors Felix Abt prefers to stay apolitical and impartial when sharing his thoughts and memories of his extraordinary seven-year sojourn. His unbiased approach to North Korea is a provocation to all those who read and believe the wacky/scandalous and horrific North Korea stories (often with dodgy sourcing) that sell so well and that people readily believe.<br /> <br />For this reason Abt’s book will never get the same praise and is bound to sell only a fraction of “Nothing to Envy. Ordinary Lives in North Korea”. The latter is by far the best-selling North Korea book even though it has not much to do with today’s “Ordinary Lives in in North Korea” but very much with the lives of the depicted 6 defectors living in the worst crisis period (during the nineties) in the worst affected industrial city (Chongjin). Thanks to Abt’s book we learn how much North Korea has changed since then. <br /><br />While he offers in his unique first-hand account insight into business interactions, he's sharing amazing observations about relations between men and women, North Koreans and foreigners, North Koreans and South Koreans and so on.<br /><br />The account is also peppered with interesting anecdotes and stories about private life that do not typically receive attention in the western media.<br /><br />This North Korea book also distinguishes itself by the 200+ photos taken by the author. Abt added more eye-opening North Korea images to a photo gallery here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/felix_abt/sets/72157639219481725/">http://www.flickr.com/photos/felix_ab...</a><br /><br />His memoir is an absolute must-read for anybody interested in this reclusive country.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17152015466367801293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1041469202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1041469202" />
    <a title="Callimaco Genovese" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33930972-callimaco-genovese"><img alt="Callimaco Genovese" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407946895p2/33930972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1041469202?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Callimaco Genovese" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Callimaco Genovese" href="/user/show/33930972-callimaco-genovese">Callimaco Genovese</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/22729010-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33930972-callimaco-genovese?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1041469202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12803597611548420824">Like probably everyone else I have been horrified and angered by what I have read of the brutal regime in North Korea. I have ranted with the best of them how the evil perpetrators of human rights violations should be brought to book for throwing a large proportion of the population into concentration camps and viciously oppressing the remainder. BUT… having just read Felix Abt’s “A Capitalist In North Korea: Seven Years in the Hermit Kingdom” I must admit to having my views rather moderated! In</span>
  <span id="freeText12803597611548420824" style="display:none">Like probably everyone else I have been horrified and angered by what I have read of the brutal regime in North Korea. I have ranted with the best of them how the evil perpetrators of human rights violations should be brought to book for throwing a large proportion of the population into concentration camps and viciously oppressing the remainder. BUT… having just read Felix Abt’s “A Capitalist In North Korea: Seven Years in the Hermit Kingdom” I must admit to having my views rather moderated! Initially I was not prepared to accept any challenge to what I thought was my educated and informed understanding of the country, but Abt’s personal account, from first-hand experience, is very compelling. While he is not a concentration camp ‘denier’ (indeed he is often openly critical of the regime) he did help me put things in perspective and realize that 99.5% of the population are ordinary people just getting on with their lives in much the same way as people the world over. If, like me, you had a simplistic “North Korea = Bad” point of view you really should check out this book and be prepared to re-consider.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12803597611548420824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_812454182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/812454182" />
    <a title="Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27348453-lawrence"><img alt="Lawrence" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/812454182?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lawrence" href="/user/show/27348453-lawrence">Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/17255166-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer812454182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6431500892952929910">Honesty Should Be Rewarded Not Punished<br/><br/>The same way I was tired and bored 20/30 years ago of books about how bad China and Vietnam were, how they were the devil and the real hell on earth, all because their ideas and ways of doing things did not fit with those of that of the west. Now more and more from the west are flocking to China and Vietnam in search for work, China owns a lot of America and all the lies that were written 20/30 years ago have been forgotten. North Korea will be no different</span>
  <span id="freeText6431500892952929910" style="display:none">Honesty Should Be Rewarded Not Punished<br /><br />The same way I was tired and bored 20/30 years ago of books about how bad China and Vietnam were, how they were the devil and the real hell on earth, all because their ideas and ways of doing things did not fit with those of that of the west. Now more and more from the west are flocking to China and Vietnam in search for work, China owns a lot of America and all the lies that were written 20/30 years ago have been forgotten. North Korea will be no different and it takes people like Felix Abt to go and actually experience it and then resist the temptation of bashing the country to bits in search for money, imagine after 7 years he could of written fake horror stories and made a fortune off of it, he would have become CNN'S favourite speaker for sure. Instead he gives an honest account of the positive and the not so positive things that he saw from an unbiast perspective, which shows throughout the whole book. <br /><br />This is also a book I feel that any business person should start reading, especially those based/ already doing business in Asia as they may well find themselves doing business in North Korea in the future. In a world were the media lies to us on a regular basis and sells us manipulated information, let's support someone who has actually written something true and unbiast. As the title says he is a capitalist, making his way through a socialist state, it is an absoluteley brilliant read, I recommend this to anyone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6431500892952929910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3515543945600494052">Loved this! Far from the usual doom and gloom you can read about North Korea, this book shows a side of the country that's much more relatable for the average Westerner. Sure, the focus is mainly on life in Pyongyang, while life in the countryside is probably much harsher (the situation is pretty much the same in my native Russia), but I really enjoyed descriptions of North Koreans' daily lives and of what it's like to do business in such an environment. Highly recommended book!</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_525785849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/525785849" />
    <a title="Jae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4973966-jae"><img alt="Jae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451878265p2/4973966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/525785849?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jae" href="/user/show/4973966-jae">Jae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/17255166-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973966-jae?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer525785849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18395182254086623934">Let me make one thing clear upfront: this is actually a three-star book. Sure, it's a little rambly and somewhat lacking in focus, but it's pretty well written (I'd even say <i>very</i> well written for a self-published tome), and more importantly, it contains a lot of information that can't be found anywhere else about the myriad little ways in which North Korea has changed since the first western books about it were written. So if that sort of thing grabs you, you really won't want to miss this book,</span>
  <span id="freeText18395182254086623934" style="display:none">Let me make one thing clear upfront: this is actually a three-star book. Sure, it's a little rambly and somewhat lacking in focus, but it's pretty well written (I'd even say <i>very</i> well written for a self-published tome), and more importantly, it contains a lot of information that can't be found anywhere else about the myriad little ways in which North Korea has changed since the first western books about it were written. So if that sort of thing grabs you, you really won't want to miss this book, and you absolutely have my blessing to buy it.<br /><br />That said, I can't quite bring myself to give the book the three stars it earned because the author comes across as such a jackass! I mean, you can trust me when I say that I'm actually <i>completely</i> receptive to the notion that all might not be doom and gloom in North Korea and that there's lots of propaganda on the western side as well, but Abt goes entirely overboard. His entire message seems to be that everyone else who has written a book about North Korea is misguided, and only <i>he</i> knows the real story. Never mind the way he slams all of the writers of <i>older</i> books about the country, Abt even manages to take potshots at more recent writers like Barbara Demick, whose work in her wonderful book of defectors' stories was painstakingly checked, cross-checked, and double-checked in the very best journalistic tradition (Abt, of course, argues against the points she makes in her book based solely on his own personal observations, but we're supposed to assume that that's somehow better). By contrast, former UK ambassador John Everard, who wrote a very recent book that <i>also</i> spoke out against the "doom and gloom" propaganda angle so common in western books about North Korea, managed to conclude that both his own observations and others' observations could be valid for different parts of the country and at different times throughout its history. For Abt, though, everybody else's work is necessarily "shaky," full of "patronizing falsehoods," and "Orwellian."<br /><br />If the pooh-poohing of other writers of books about North Korea were the only issue, I probably could have overlooked it easily enough without wanting to throw the book at the wall. But Abt also smugly gives most of the westerners he worked with in the country an even worse sort of treatment, talking smack about them while only thinly disguising their identities so that readers can easily figure out who they are in real life (he goes so far as to talk about what one guy wrote on his Facebook page, and sneers at the way another was constantly looking for photo-ops with various dignitaries so that he could put the pictures on his website). The book also full of back-patting about how awesome he himself is by contrast: how he's able to recognize all sorts of cultural subtleties that other people fail to recognize, and how he's <i>so</i> much better a businessman as a result (there's even some musing about why no one ever asked him to do any spying while he was there, which made me laugh out loud). And as if that weren't bad enough, there's also a chapter filled with bizarrely worded "compliments" of various North Korean women, calling them "pretty and affable" or "charming and clever," in a way that seemed to be trying a little too hard to make it sound like he wasn't just salivating over them sexually but respected them for their brains too. (Thankfully, there are only a few moments of <i>blatant</i> salivating, although one of them is pretty eew-inducing: a picture of a woman he knew with the caption "Had there been 'Miss Juche' elections in North Korea, all foreigners would have elected this lady as Miss Juche.") And okay, maybe this is petty, but as a German speaker myself, I was also rubbed the wrong way by all of the Germanisms and other bits of odd English in the book ("lended support to the project," "the ideological bend," "after the many sleepless nights," "it allowed this only, if paid and declared as a gift," etc.), which would have been a problem easily solved by getting a native speaker to carefully edit it rather than arrogantly assuming it was of course perfect as it was.<br /><br />So I knocked off a star for all of that crap. All in all, Abt comes across as someone you'd want to slap if you knew him in person, and that made reading his book, regardless of its interesting and valid insights, a real chore. Yes, western readers of books about North Korea will certainly want to read it, but please be forewarned and prepare to feel annoyed with the author when you do. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18395182254086623934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Daniel Bellino-Zwicke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12474769-daniel-bellino-zwicke"><img alt="Daniel Bellino-Zwicke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442957215p2/12474769.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Bellino-Zwicke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Bellino-Zwicke" href="/user/show/12474769-daniel-bellino-zwicke">Daniel Bellino-Zwicke</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1013819752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2565211125075448088">It’s refreshing to find a book about North Korea that isn’t full of demonizing hyperbole. A true insight into a country that is largely misunderstood and misreported in the West. Mr Abt’s very personal experiences lend authenticity to a well-balanced account of both the bigger political and business picture in the republic, and day to day life for ‘regular’ people.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1035198546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1035198546" />
    <a title="Jan Oesterreich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34260859-jan-oesterreich"><img alt="Jan Oesterreich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408889092p2/34260859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1035198546?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan Oesterreich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan Oesterreich" href="/user/show/34260859-jan-oesterreich">Jan Oesterreich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035198546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17825210689199871910">Having read several other books on North Korea already, I found this book extremely interesting, easy readable on one hand while also offering an in-depth view on the historical, political and of course the business parameters which define the current state of this isolated country. <br/><br/>Felix Abt offers a well-balanced approach to explain the self-perception of the North Korean people and their country, without judging in the typical political way which we see so often with other authors. This is ju</span>
  <span id="freeText17825210689199871910" style="display:none">Having read several other books on North Korea already, I found this book extremely interesting, easy readable on one hand while also offering an in-depth view on the historical, political and of course the business parameters which define the current state of this isolated country. <br /><br />Felix Abt offers a well-balanced approach to explain the self-perception of the North Korean people and their country, without judging in the typical political way which we see so often with other authors. This is just to name one of the many facets of this book but for me personally it was the most important. It is clear that the author's description is shaped by the experience of having lived and worked in North Korea for several years. So this book is not offering a so called 'objective journalistic' description. <br /><br />However, it is exactly this experience (probably a unique one in the way that only a very small number of western managers so far have put themselves in the position from which they had to build up a profitable business operation, let alone in a sensitive and highly regulated field such as pharmaceuticals)which makes the "Capitalist in North Korea" a refreshing and highly informative piece of literature for every one who is interested in first-hand information from the inside of North Korea. <br /><br />For someone like me who has build up a local operational business entity from the scratch too - but in comparison to Mr. Abt's location in a much more convenient business environment here in Asia - these seven years which the author has not endured but actively shaped for himself and the success of his company deserve my greatest respect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17825210689199871910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1026341240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026341240" />
    <a title="Gladys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22012865-gladys"><img alt="Gladys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395161143p2/22012865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026341240?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gladys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gladys" href="/user/show/22012865-gladys">Gladys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22012865-gladys?shelf=exclusive">exclusive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026341240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6405297243888328822">It was greatly refreshing to read a first-hand account of what is really happening inside North Korea at the moment, rather than second-hand accounts of what was happening 15 or 20 years ago. Most of what I have read previously has been coming from one viewpoint and has focused on the shockingly grim years of the 1990s, when the country was ravaged by natural disasters, famine and millions died from starvation. I found Abt’s version of contemporary North Korea and its willingness to face change </span>
  <span id="freeText6405297243888328822" style="display:none">It was greatly refreshing to read a first-hand account of what is really happening inside North Korea at the moment, rather than second-hand accounts of what was happening 15 or 20 years ago. Most of what I have read previously has been coming from one viewpoint and has focused on the shockingly grim years of the 1990s, when the country was ravaged by natural disasters, famine and millions died from starvation. I found Abt’s version of contemporary North Korea and its willingness to face change greatly encouraging. It would be nice to think that a few copies could make their way into the upper reaches of the White House and open a few eyes there!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6405297243888328822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1041035213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1041035213" />
    <a title="Victoria Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33810515-victoria-robinson"><img alt="Victoria Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407618649p2/33810515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1041035213?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Robinson" href="/user/show/33810515-victoria-robinson">Victoria Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/22729010-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33810515-victoria-robinson?shelf=geography">geography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1041035213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3844640502334092820">I have read a great many biographies of trail-blazers and Felix Abt’s story of being a capitalist in that oh-so communist nation of North Korea is as intriguing and inspiring as any. His has an unwavering belief in capitalism as a potent and positive agent for change and development. I think people of any political or economic belief cannot fail to see after reading Mr Abt’s book that ‘free-enterprise’ is not necessarily a dirty word but can be a force for good under the direction of responsible</span>
  <span id="freeText3844640502334092820" style="display:none">I have read a great many biographies of trail-blazers and Felix Abt’s story of being a capitalist in that oh-so communist nation of North Korea is as intriguing and inspiring as any. His has an unwavering belief in capitalism as a potent and positive agent for change and development. I think people of any political or economic belief cannot fail to see after reading Mr Abt’s book that ‘free-enterprise’ is not necessarily a dirty word but can be a force for good under the direction of responsible and positive entrepreneurs like Mr Abt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3844640502334092820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1027495594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1027495594" />
    <a title="Stacey Young" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33984315-stacey-young"><img alt="Stacey Young" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408099698p2/33984315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1027495594?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey Young" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey Young" href="/user/show/33984315-stacey-young">Stacey Young</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1027495594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12567266023610976560">An entirely fresh perspective on North Korea and therefore a must-read!<br/><br/>“A Capitalist in North Korea: My Seven Years in the Hermit Kingdom” by Felix Abt has its detractors and you may not agree with everything (or anything) he says, but there is no doubt that this is a book written from a unique first-hand experience as a "capitalist" in an arch communist country and I believe it deserves to be read for that reason as much as any other.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1033139342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1033139342" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26113400-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1033139342?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/26113400-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/22729010-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1033139342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer500022372957298117">North Korea has been in the news a lot recently. Of course, much of the attention has been negative and rightly so--it's sort of a mess, one with threats of missile launches, nuclear weapons, and allegations of serious human rights violations. I was curious to read about the country and its people from the perspective of someone who had once, at least sort of, been an insider. I found it here! Felix Abt has written a comprehensive, honest piece about life in North Korea. He truly seems to write </span>
  <span id="freeText500022372957298117" style="display:none">North Korea has been in the news a lot recently. Of course, much of the attention has been negative and rightly so--it's sort of a mess, one with threats of missile launches, nuclear weapons, and allegations of serious human rights violations. I was curious to read about the country and its people from the perspective of someone who had once, at least sort of, been an insider. I found it here! Felix Abt has written a comprehensive, honest piece about life in North Korea. He truly seems to write objectively, which is refreshing. His anecdotes and observations are so interesting, especially to someone who knows nothing about the region. Overall a great read and highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="500022372957298117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1002386116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002386116" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32874180-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404760551p2/32874180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002386116?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/32874180-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/17255166-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002386116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8805507947927305810">I’ve always admired adventurers and pioneers and here I came across an amazing one penetrating fortress North Korea. Until now I’ve read only about starvation and concentration camps and was made believe that’s about all the ‘Hermit Kingdom’ is about, but the “Capitalist in North Korea” opened my eyes and showed me that most “Ordinary Lives in North Korea” are not as horrific as I’ve been told before. It’s a must-read for everybody seriously interested in this country.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1040337834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1040337834" />
    <a title="Bruno Ferri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34055881-bruno-ferri"><img alt="Bruno Ferri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408326116p2/34055881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1040337834?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruno Ferri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruno Ferri" href="/user/show/34055881-bruno-ferri">Bruno Ferri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/22729010-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34055881-bruno-ferri?shelf=personal">personal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34055881-bruno-ferri?shelf=world-s-read">world-s-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1040337834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7927868504879342422">If it does nothing else “A Capitalist In North Korea” confirms that man is by nature a trader. That even under the strictest state controls private enterprises will emerge and people will find ways of eking out their existence by buying and selling. I was fascinated by this first-hand account of what is happening in North Korea and found the daring exploits of Felix Abt in the face of all kinds of difficulties truly inspiring. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1115716362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1115716362" />
    <a title="Kathryn Broderick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37322719-kathryn-broderick"><img alt="Kathryn Broderick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959750p2/37322719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1115716362?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn Broderick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn Broderick" href="/user/show/37322719-kathryn-broderick">Kathryn Broderick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1115716362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10765947790096343407">There are many who, on a relentless diet of Western condemnation of all things North Korean, cannot stomach any view that does not unequivocally vilify the country. It seems to those with this mind-set that anyone, even if they roundly criticize the country’s governance, are characterized as having been blindly taken in by propaganda or labeled as a stooge or apologist if they attempt to cast an accurate light on the actual, contemporary state of affairs in the country rather than unconditionall</span>
  <span id="freeText10765947790096343407" style="display:none">There are many who, on a relentless diet of Western condemnation of all things North Korean, cannot stomach any view that does not unequivocally vilify the country. It seems to those with this mind-set that anyone, even if they roundly criticize the country’s governance, are characterized as having been blindly taken in by propaganda or labeled as a stooge or apologist if they attempt to cast an accurate light on the actual, contemporary state of affairs in the country rather than unconditionally trashing everything to do with it.<br /><br />Felix Abt finds himself in just such a position; labeled by detractors as a ‘regime supporter’ for his work “A Capitalist in North Korea: My Seven Years in the Hermit Kingdom”. But, such a label is not merely inaccurate, but shows that those who are leveling it have missed the point of the book and read it unwilling to challenge their pre-conceptions. If one was to try and put a single label on Mr Abt, it would be far more germane to use John Feffer’s ‘agent of change’. Mr Feffer, as a widely respected writer, is undoubtedly better informed and less tendentious than the average reader and is able to recognize Felix Abt’s role in helping to bring responsible capitalism to North Korea and to try and improve safety and conditions for ordinary workers.<br /> <br />The business school that Mr Abt co-founded in North Korea taught putative business executives to build companies which would in themselves bring about positive change by creating jobs and generating income for workers. But it went a lot further, imbuing the students with the social and ethical responsibility which goes hand-in-hand with good business practice: paying decent wages, doing away with child labor, ensuring workers’ safety, protecting the environment, respecting contractual obligations. Several years on, the growth of private enterprise and associated job creation can be clearly seen in the country along with the implementation of the good practices taught at the school. Some of the school’s graduates also introduced truly pioneering business concepts. One, a bank director, introduced the first debit card and another became the CEO of the first advertising company. The latter might not sound that remarkable until one understands that formerly advertising had been banned as “anti-socialist” and is, therefore just one very tangible example of Mr Abt’s role not as a ‘regime supporter’, but an ‘agent of change’.<br /> <br />As those who have read the book will know Felix Abt was also president of the first foreign chamber of commerce in North Korea. This became a significant forum for change as he lobbied decision makers for reforms and the establishment of a level playing field for all businesses. The organization was increasingly listened to and changes implemented by those in power helped facilitate the development of businesses and all the associated benefits.<br /> <br />“A Capitalist in North Korea” contains many further examples of how Abt helped bring about change in the country; not to help line the pockets or enhance the power of the elites, but to improve the lot of workers and ordinary residents of the country:<br /><br />He sold equipment, specifically safety gear, to mining concerns to modernize and improve the working conditions of the workforce and as the CEO of the first foreign-invested pharmaceutical factory the enterprise was the first to achieve an internationally acknowledged quality standard recognized by the WHO. Strange to many, and counter to the cynical, hard-nosed, profit driven image of foreign capitalists he shared the knowledge with his local competitors to help increase quality standards generally. <br /><br />Neither of these two examples in any way helped the regime in itself; either its members personally or in terms of control of the populace: members of the elite weren’t in danger from dying from working down mines nor were they likely to suffer from the consequences of treating illness with poor quality and ineffective medicines (they had ready access to expensive, imported brands). Doubtlessly people’s lives were not only improved, but also many lives were actually saved.<br /><br />Labels are not always helpful, they are by definition simplistic, but if one has to allot one to Felix Abt is ‘regime supporter’ fair or accurate for someone who is critical, tried to bring about many changes and did nothing to benefit the members of the elites? Or in the light of what he actually did in North Korea is not ‘pioneer’ or John Feffer’s ‘agent of change’ far more pertinent and, indeed, factual?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10765947790096343407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13398653-kodzo-selormey?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574648948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15230196730754715744">I am not sure who Mr Abt has written this book for. He seems to assume that the reader will have no knowledge of North Korea, its history and people other than what they get from the Television news and therefore the message throughout the book is North Korea isn't that bad. The people aren't all crazy and the government stupid. <br/><br/><br/>The other message that comes across loud and clear is that people should have listened more to Felix when he told them stuff. <br/><br/>All of this gives the book a tone of mother</span>
  <span id="freeText15230196730754715744" style="display:none">I am not sure who Mr Abt has written this book for. He seems to assume that the reader will have no knowledge of North Korea, its history and people other than what they get from the Television news and therefore the message throughout the book is North Korea isn't that bad. The people aren't all crazy and the government stupid. <br /><br /><br />The other message that comes across loud and clear is that people should have listened more to Felix when he told them stuff. <br /><br />All of this gives the book a tone of mother knows best, which is annoying. This is also not helped by the attacks on other writers such as the excellent Barbara Demick and on individuals who he worked with.<br /><br />However he does provide a fascinating insight into how business is done and the working and social relationships between Koreans and Expats, which I have not seen detailed in any of the books I have read about North Korea. It is worthwhile reading for this alone. </span>

<div id="review_1115257255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1115257255" />
    <a title="James Hanson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34274920-james-hanson"><img alt="James Hanson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408924645p2/34274920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1115257255?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Hanson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Hanson" href="/user/show/34274920-james-hanson">James Hanson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/22729010-a-capitalist-in-north-korea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1115257255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7486033046519419703">I thoroughly recommend this book as a very accessible and believable account of what life in North Korea is really like. The author, Felix Abt, does not try to put a gloss on the failings of the totalitarian regime, but you feel you are finally getting a balanced view of what is really happening behind all the secrecy. As he points out much of what we have heard before only looks at a particularly difficult period in North Korea in the 1990s (20 years ago) and nearly all reporting since then has</span>
  <span id="freeText7486033046519419703" style="display:none">I thoroughly recommend this book as a very accessible and believable account of what life in North Korea is really like. The author, Felix Abt, does not try to put a gloss on the failings of the totalitarian regime, but you feel you are finally getting a balanced view of what is really happening behind all the secrecy. As he points out much of what we have heard before only looks at a particularly difficult period in North Korea in the 1990s (20 years ago) and nearly all reporting since then has been coloured by preconceptions from this period. Mr Abt brings us up to date and reveals a North Korea that is permitting change, slowly, but under its young foreign-educated leader, Kim Jong-un, there seems to be a willingness to embrace new ideas and ways of doing things. It will be interesting to see, as Mr Abt suggests, whether the North Koreans follow the models of Vietnam and China.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7486033046519419703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1194023053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194023053" />
    <a title="Ryan Rommann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10398400-ryan-rommann"><img alt="Ryan Rommann" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194023053?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Rommann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Rommann" href="/user/show/10398400-ryan-rommann">Ryan Rommann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194023053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6973969336971415280">This book is close to being North Korean propaganda. There is virtually no criticism of the DPRK government, but rather Abt blames everything on Western sanctions that have arisen only because the DPRK is trying to defend itself from an "imperialist US." Even the language and word choice is alarmingly close to that approved by the WPK, with a hint of reverence for "the Dear Leader."<br/><br/>Abt did spend seven years in a slightly larger bubble than the one experienced by insulated foreign tourists. That </span>
  <span id="freeText6973969336971415280" style="display:none">This book is close to being North Korean propaganda. There is virtually no criticism of the DPRK government, but rather Abt blames everything on Western sanctions that have arisen only because the DPRK is trying to defend itself from an "imperialist US." Even the language and word choice is alarmingly close to that approved by the WPK, with a hint of reverence for "the Dear Leader."<br /><br />Abt did spend seven years in a slightly larger bubble than the one experienced by insulated foreign tourists. That makes for some interesting reading and challenging perspectives. But if one wants a genuine account of North Korea, there are numerous better books written by actual North Koreans that have seen behind the curtain. Those books, for the most part, paint a far, far less rosy picture than the one painted by Abt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6973969336971415280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1100936800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100936800" />
    <a title="Elektra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34151631-elektra"><img alt="Elektra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447318429p2/34151631.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1010018372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010018372?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter Mckinskey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter Mckinskey" href="/user/show/30151928-peter-mckinskey">Peter Mckinskey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010018372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11605610904287445556">This book had my interest from the start. It is a combination of true life stories and realistic descriptions of the life of North Koreans. The pace is enjoyable, and the length of the book is perfect. Felix Abt did a great job of accomplishing what he had saw and learn while he was trying to do business in North Korea. This book is somewhat refreshing as a contrast to the doom and gloom of nearly every other DPRK-based book I've seen, which focus so heavily on refugees and political prisoners.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1074898092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074898092" />
    <a title="Alek Sigley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32970994-alek-sigley"><img alt="Alek Sigley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549866108p2/32970994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1074898092?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alek Sigley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alek Sigley" href="/user/show/32970994-alek-sigley">Alek Sigley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074898092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15194556073019691524">Much of the English language literature on North Korea is little more than polemics. Whether journalism, academic texts (often written by armchair academics who don't speak any Korean), memoirs, or fiction, these writings merely stereotype North Korea as the irrational, despotic "other" to the West's rational and ordered self. They are also inextricably linked to the US and its allies' policies of isolating the North, serving as the ideological rationalisation for such policies by portraying Nor</span>
  <span id="freeText15194556073019691524" style="display:none">Much of the English language literature on North Korea is little more than polemics. Whether journalism, academic texts (often written by armchair academics who don't speak any Korean), memoirs, or fiction, these writings merely stereotype North Korea as the irrational, despotic "other" to the West's rational and ordered self. They are also inextricably linked to the US and its allies' policies of isolating the North, serving as the ideological rationalisation for such policies by portraying North Korea in simplistic terms of evil and darkness that one cannot reason or negotiate with.<br /><br />And that's exactly why Felix Abt's A Capitalist in North Korea is such a breath of fresh air. Based on Abt's extensive on the ground experience as a businessperson and expatriate resident of Pyongyang (which none of the armchair pundits have), it portrays both the good, and bad of living and working in North Korea. <br /><br />It was also refreshing to see North Koreans portrayed as individuals, each with their own unique personalities, hopes and dreams—a perspective which is sorely missing in most of the other accounts of North Korea.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book for anyone with a serious interest in North Korea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15194556073019691524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1262548596948405575" style="display:none">A fascinating and eye opening book from start to finish. Please read this if your idea of North Korea is that everything about it is bad and evil. Felix Abt’s wonderfully informed version of real life in North Korea challenges nearly everything you will have read about the country before. I was fascinated not only with his stories of trying to set up and run all sorts of businesses, but also with the anecdotes about everyday life in North Korea. You really get to see how people actually live day to day and it makes you remember that a country is all about its people, whatever the politics and the sensational headlines.</span>

<div id="review_2166349152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2166349152" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/348164-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464394238p2/348164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2166349152?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/348164-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2166349152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13149362946359095466">I like the idea of this book much more than it's implementation. I enjoy anything that looks at North Korea from more than a military perspective, but it felt a little bit to me like Abt drank the regime's Kool-Aid and portrayed only the better side of things. Equally frustrating and entwined with this issue was that he was reporting anecdotes from the most privileged part of society and extrapolating to suggest that all of society was like the small bubble that he lived in. While he acknowledge</span>
  <span id="freeText13149362946359095466" style="display:none">I like the idea of this book much more than it's implementation. I enjoy anything that looks at North Korea from more than a military perspective, but it felt a little bit to me like Abt drank the regime's Kool-Aid and portrayed only the better side of things. Equally frustrating and entwined with this issue was that he was reporting anecdotes from the most privileged part of society and extrapolating to suggest that all of society was like the small bubble that he lived in. While he acknowledges hunger in his chapter on 'feeding the people' it seems like he forgets the inequalities he notes here throughout the rest of the book.<br /><br />Abt's condescending commentary on other foreigners while touting his own accomplishments were distracting. I struggle with his portrayal of aid workers trying not to succeed because then they'd work themselves out of a job. (There are plenty of disasters and plenty of need in the world to keep aid employees at work forever... there's no need for this cynicism. <br /><br />I do agree, in part, with his strongly held belief that a capitalist push and the opening of markets are the only things that can ultimately change this regime. However, the reality that economic sanctions and the Kaesong industrial center are also among the only political tools open to the US and South Korea is a complexity in the formula that Abt misses entirely.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13149362946359095466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1269625549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1269625549" />
    <a title="Suzi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3589084-suzi"><img alt="Suzi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1269625549?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzi" href="/user/show/3589084-suzi">Suzi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3589084-suzi?shelf=korea">korea</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1269625549" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6940998913927560355">This should have been a really good insightful book. The tone was very annoying. Felix seems to be the only person who knows or understands anything. The insights might also have been good if more timely. Much would seem to have changed. I persevered through approximately the first half then just skimmed the second half. Uncomfortable with how "pro-North Korea" he seemed to be, that is so much at odds with other reads, accounts and lectures. But it is another perspective on a country few have vi</span>
  <span id="freeText6940998913927560355" style="display:none">This should have been a really good insightful book. The tone was very annoying. Felix seems to be the only person who knows or understands anything. The insights might also have been good if more timely. Much would seem to have changed. I persevered through approximately the first half then just skimmed the second half. Uncomfortable with how "pro-North Korea" he seemed to be, that is so much at odds with other reads, accounts and lectures. But it is another perspective on a country few have visited, even fewer have worked in. So I guess if you are really interested give it a go, maybe the tone won't be so annoying to you.</span>

    <a title="Suzanne Jernigan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34248736-suzanne-jernigan"><img alt="Suzanne Jernigan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408844812p2/34248736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1118022008?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne Jernigan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne Jernigan" href="/user/show/34248736-suzanne-jernigan">Suzanne Jernigan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34248736-suzanne-jernigan?shelf=goodread">goodread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1118022008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8002825090679369517">I am full of admiration for Felix Abt, not only for his courage in being the ‘Capitalist in North Korea’ , but also for writing a book that clearly flies in the face of just about everything else we have read in the West about the ‘hermit kingdom’. This is a book you must read if you want to understand exactly what North Korea is all about, warts and all: put your prejudices to one side and be prepared to have your pre-conceptions turned on their head.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3283854114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3283854114" />
    <a title="Bagus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32952691-bagus"><img alt="Bagus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603964873p2/32952691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3283854114?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bagus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bagus" href="/user/show/32952691-bagus">Bagus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32952691-bagus?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32952691-bagus?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32952691-bagus?shelf=references">references</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32952691-bagus?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32952691-bagus?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32952691-bagus?shelf=korea">korea</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3283854114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2463432387200517527"><i>"It's a dream that hasn't been quite realized, but I remain optimistic. If the New York Philharmonic could be so well received in North Korea, then I place my hope in the coming winds of change."</i><br/><br/>This is the book which will surely be hated by most Western media which promote the common narrative of North Korea as a country which follow military-first policy (<i>songun</i>) and starving its own people in order to build its nuclear arms. And not to mention to how most media outlets and international NGOs </span>
  <span id="freeText2463432387200517527" style="display:none"><i>"It's a dream that hasn't been quite realized, but I remain optimistic. If the New York Philharmonic could be so well received in North Korea, then I place my hope in the coming winds of change."</i><br /><br />This is the book which will surely be hated by most Western media which promote the common narrative of North Korea as a country which follow military-first policy (<i>songun</i>) and starving its own people in order to build its nuclear arms. And not to mention to how most media outlets and international NGOs which routinely demonised North Korean regime as a staunch human rights abuser with countless Nazi-style concentration camps around the country. We could not deny that it is true that North Korea was pursuing to build inter-continental ballistic missiles (ICBM) and also there are victims of concentration camps among defectors, but it should be noted that most of the narratives built around North Korea are based on the accounts of defectors who mostly left North Korea amid the great famine in the 1990s, or in more sophisticated North Korean term would be called: the Arduous March.<br /><br />Indeed the Arduous March has been a turning point for a gradual reform introduced in North Korea post-2000, something that Felix Abt, a Swiss entrepreneur, has been trying to point over and over in this memoir of him. As an entrepreneur who has lived in various developing countries in Africa, the Middle East, and especially Vietnam in the 1990s, he is quite familiar with the gradual reform that the government of Vietnam has been introducing after the Đổi Mới Policy (Renovation) prior to his appointment as the representative of ABB group in the Democratic People's Republic of Korea (DPRK). Perhaps it is his understanding of the orient which has led him to pursue a different pathway than most Europeans did in his approach to the North Korean bureaucracy during the time of his tenure building up Pyongyang Business School and later while becoming the Director of PyongSu pharmaceutical company until 2009.<br /><br />Probably this book will awe us with hard-to-believe data. If we try to understand the DPRK from the bestselling <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6178648.Nothing_to_Envy_Ordinary_Lives_in_North_Korea" title="Nothing to Envy Ordinary Lives in North Korea by Barbara Demick" rel="nofollow noopener">Nothing to Envy: Ordinary Lives in North Korea</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11797365.Escape_from_Camp_14_One_Man_s_Remarkable_Odyssey_from_North_Korea_to_Freedom_in_the_West" title="Escape from Camp 14 One Man's Remarkable Odyssey from North Korea to Freedom in the West by Blaine Harden" rel="nofollow noopener">Escape from Camp 14: One Man's Remarkable Odyssey from North Korea to Freedom in the West</a>, we will probably only witness the bad parts of the DPRK on how the state abuse the citizens and deprive them of their basic human rights. On par with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22892099.North_Korea_Confidential_Private_Markets__Fashion_Trends__Prison_Camps__Dissenters_and_Defectors" title="North Korea Confidential Private Markets, Fashion Trends, Prison Camps, Dissenters and Defectors by Daniel Tudor" rel="nofollow noopener">North Korea Confidential: Private Markets, Fashion Trends, Prison Camps, Dissenters and Defectors</a>, I think this book could provide us with fresher account of how and why the DPRK regime has not collapsed yet until now even though it has been threatened several times from the outside through the sanctions imposed by the United Nations and the declaration of the DPRK of <i>axis of evil</i> by the Bush regime. <br /><br />"Business strategy, business plan, marketing, human resources management? What the heck is that?" were the first few questions that Felix Abt encountered during the time he first introduced the concept of business at the Pyongyang Business School in early 2000s. Those questions sound innocent to us who might take for granted how the capitalist economy has shaped our day-to-day situation, but it showed the gestures from the elite inside Pyongyang to slowly embrace reforms from centrally-oriented economy to market-oriented one. The question would be, to what extend the DPRK regime is willing to embrace the reform and what kind of comparison that we could see from the reforms which had been taken in the previous decades by Vietnam and China? The political scientist Ben Kerkvliet has shown in his paper how in Vietnam the pressure from villagers and farmers pushed the party onto the path of reform after food shortages in the early 1980s. If the similar case could happen, then the change might be initiated from the bottom to up and subsequently accepted by the party.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2463432387200517527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
